        <p class="date">
         Mon Feb 03, 2014 at 06:16 AM PST
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2014/02/03/1271430/-25-Images-of-Markets-Regulating-Themselves" id="titleHref">
          25 Images of Markets "Regulating Themselves"
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/akadjian">
          akadjian
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=319630&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/02/03/1271430/-25-Images-of-Markets-Regulating-Themselves" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text='25 Images of Markets "Regulating Themselves"' data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/02/03/1271430/-25-Images-of-Markets-Regulating-Themselves" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="203" data-story_id="1271430" href="/story/2014/02/03/1271430/-25-Images-of-Markets-Regulating-Themselves#comments">
           203 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <p>
          When economists talk about how a market "regulates itself," what they mean is that markets reach an equilibrium between supply and demand.
         </p>
         <p>
          This says nothing about whether or not this equilibrium will be a good thing for society. It simply states that if consumers choose what to buy and producers choose what to sell and how to produce it, the market settles on a product distribution and prices.
         </p>
         <p>
          Lately, many people I know have argued that "free markets" mean something more. They see markets as ethically right or ethically moral, meaning pursuit of profit always somehow leads to a greater good.
         </p>
         <p>
          Unfortunately, morality isn't built into markets.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/child-labor-sm_zpse67cfcab.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo child-labor-sm_zpse67cfcab.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/child-labor-sm_zpse67cfcab.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Markets were fine with child labor and slavery. Both were viewed simply as cheap sources of labor. It wasn't until people fought against child labor and slavery that these things became unacceptable in a market (at least in most Western countries).
         </p>
         <p>
          This is why markets must be subject to other forces such as ethics and government if we want them to work for the benefit of the many (not just a select few).
         </p>
         <p>
          Now you may know all this and if that's the case, you're ahead of the game.
         </p>
         <p>
          However, many of us know people who have either bought into the claim that government is the only thing standing between us and a truly "free" market or are on the fence about the role of government.
         </p>
         <p>
          Here are a few examples I've found that make a convincing case for regulations and good government.
          <br/>
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          <strong>
           2014 Oxfam report "85 people own more than the poorest 3.5 billion people on the planet"
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          This statistic from
          <a href="http://www.oxfam.org/en/policy/working-for-the-few-economic-inequality">
           Oxfam
          </a>
          is staggering. Just 85 people, the top 0.00000001 percent, own as much as the poorest 3.5 billion people on the planet.
         </p>
         <p>
          Oxfam's concern is not only that wealth is concentrated at the top, but that it will remain this way, passed down from generation to generation like royalty.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/oxfam-85_zpsb97970d3.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo oxfam-85_zpsb97970d3.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/oxfam-85_zpsb97970d3.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          According to Nick Galasso, co-author of the report:
          <br/>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          "High levels of inequality actually corrode democratic processes. What we have seen across the globe and what the report documents is how wealth concentration is used to influence the political process to create laws and regulations that benefit the rich over everyone else."
         </blockquote>
         <strong>
          2014 West Virginia chemical spill
         </strong>
         <p>
          Freedom Industries allowed to act freely (left alone by the EPA for 20 years) lets 7,500 gallons of MCHM (4-methylcyclohexane methanol) into the Elk River. 300,000 lose water for days.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2014-freedom-water_zps1e17a0d2.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2014-freedom-water_zps1e17a0d2.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2014-freedom-water_zps1e17a0d2.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Montani semper liberi, Joe Manchin III, West Virginia's junior senator
          <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/2014/01/19/us/chemical-spill-muddies-picture-in-a-state-wary-of-regulations.html">
           said
          </a>
          arguing for "freer markets" at an event sponsored by the American Coalition for Clean Coal Electricity after the spill, Mountaineers are always free.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2013 Bangladesh garment factory collapse
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          1,132 people killed, 2,500 injured, 300 missing
          <br/>
          Minimum wage for garment workers = $40/month
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2013-bangladesh-factory-collapse-01_zpsd7923d72.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2013-bangladesh-factory-collapse-01_zpsd7923d72.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2013-bangladesh-factory-collapse-01_zpsd7923d72.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Months later, little has changed and the South Asian country
          <a href="http://www.cnn.com/2013/10/24/opinion/bangladesh-garment-workers/">
           continues to mourn the deaths of workers
          </a>
          in other avoidable incidents.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2013-bangladesh-factory-collapse-02_zps6b7f45dc.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2013-bangladesh-factory-collapse-02_zps6b7f45dc.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2013-bangladesh-factory-collapse-02_zps6b7f45dc.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2013 West Fertilizer Company explosion in Texas
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          15 killed, 160 injured.
         </p>
         <p>
          Texas law allows fertilizer storage facilities to operate without any liability insurance, even when they store hazardous materials.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2013-west-texas-fertilizer-plant-explosion_zpsd46c57d0.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2013-west-texas-fertilizer-plant-explosion_zpsd46c57d0.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2013-west-texas-fertilizer-plant-explosion_zpsd46c57d0.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2012 Libor price fixing scandal
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          Possibly the biggest price-fixing scandal ever affecting upwards of $500 trillion of financial instruments.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2012-libor-scandal_zps04942acc.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2012-libor-scandal_zps04942acc.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2012-libor-scandal_zps04942acc.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          By the time litigation is through, its estimated 16 banks may face up to $35 billion in civil settlements in addition to other regulatory fines.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2012 Pink Slime
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          We find out that what we're eating in our beef looks like this:
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2012-pink-slime_zps383b90a2.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2012-pink-slime_zps383b90a2.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2012-pink-slime_zps383b90a2.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          The name used in the meat industry is lean finely textured beef (LFTB). Hmmm.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2012 HSBC launders Mexican drug cartel money
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          And this is only the second biggest banking scandal of 2012 because of the Libor price fixing. JP Morgan losing $5.8 billion on a derivatives trade was a distant third.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2012-hsbc-money-laundering_zpsca789a92.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2012-hsbc-money-laundering_zpsca789a92.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2012-hsbc-money-laundering_zpsca789a92.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2011 Newscorp hacking scandal
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          Newscorp employees engage in phone hacking and police bribery to get stories.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2011-murdoch-time-mag_zps62d3c21b.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2011-murdoch-time-mag_zps62d3c21b.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2011-murdoch-time-mag_zps62d3c21b.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2010 Deepwater Horizon Oil Spill
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          11 dead. 4.9 million barrels of oil spilled into Gulf of Mexico.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2010-deepwater-horizon-02_zpsaf7757c2.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2010-deepwater-horizon-02_zpsaf7757c2.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2010-deepwater-horizon-02_zpsaf7757c2.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          $37-90 billion in cleanup costs. Billions more estimated in economic and environmental impact.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2010-deepwater-horizon-01_zps513e3558.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2010-deepwater-horizon-01_zps513e3558.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2010-deepwater-horizon-01_zps513e3558.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2010 Chilean miners trapped in collapsed mine
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          Between 2004 and 2010, the firm
          <a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/southamerica/chile/7966590/Families-of-trapped-Chilean-miners-to-sue-mining-firm.html">
           accumulated 42 fines
          </a>
          from various Chilean safety bodies for failing to protect its workers.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2010-chilean-miners_zps8a039753.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2010-chilean-miners_zps8a039753.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2010-chilean-miners_zps8a039753.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          "They never carried out the most fundamental adjustments needed to avoid disasters like what we're seeing today," Vincelot Tobar, risk assessor who resigned in 2009 because the company failed to carry out his recommendations.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2009 Queensland Oil Spill
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://web.archive.org/web/20090316002358/http://www.news.com.au/heraldsun/story/0,21985,25187797-662,00.html">
           Improperly stowed cargo dislodged
          </a>
          from the deck damaging other cargo and containers onboard causing various substances to spill into the ocean.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2009_queensland_oil_spill_01_zps8154fcc7.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2009_queensland_oil_spill_01_zps8154fcc7.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2009_queensland_oil_spill_01_zps8154fcc7.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Cost: $34 million (Australian dollars) cleanup, economy impact $10 million
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2009_queensland_oil_spill_02_zps59ae4b47.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2009_queensland_oil_spill_02_zps59ae4b47.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2009_queensland_oil_spill_02_zps59ae4b47.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2008 Lehman Brothers collapse, sub-prime mortgage crisis, and global recession
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          8 years after Graham-Leach-Bliley legislation deregulates the financial services industry.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2008-lehman-bros_zps8f50fb86.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2008-lehman-bros_zps8f50fb86.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2008-lehman-bros_zps8f50fb86.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Cost: $475 billion authorized in TARP payment, global recession, continuing too big to fail philosophy
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2008-lehman-bros-cartoon_zpse5b4fefb.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2008-lehman-bros-cartoon_zpse5b4fefb.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2008-lehman-bros-cartoon_zpse5b4fefb.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2007 Aqua Dots Recall
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          The toy's coating contains a chemical that, once ingested, converts into the toxic "date rape" drug GHB, or gamma hydroxybutyrate causing children to become comatose, develop respiratory depression, or have seizures.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2007-aquadots-recall_zps05a4c28b.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2007-aquadots-recall_zps05a4c28b.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2007-aquadots-recall_zps05a4c28b.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Spin Master, the company making Aqua Dots, identified the problem on October 17, 2007 after several reports of kids getting sick.
         </p>
         <p>
          They continued selling the product until November 7, 2007, when the U.S. Consumer Product Safety Commission (CPSC) contacted them after receiving reports. At this point, Spin Master issued a "voluntary" recall.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2006 Trafigura Dumps Toxic Waste on Ivory Coast
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          In 2006, the Dutch oil and shipping company Trafigura, chartered a ship called the Probo Koala, to offload toxic waste at numerous sites around the city of Abijan, Ivory Coast. Trafigura was seeking to avoid paying a 1,000 per cubic meter disposal charge in Amsterdam.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2006-probo-koala_zps1f4518a4.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2006-probo-koala_zps1f4518a4.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2006-probo-koala_zps1f4518a4.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Gases released by these chemicals claimed the lives of 17 and injured more than 30,000. Injuries ranged from mild headaches to severe lung and skin burns.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2006-trafigura-burns_zpsd195b99e.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2006-trafigura-burns_zpsd195b99e.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2006-trafigura-burns_zpsd195b99e.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2006 E. Coli outbreak from contaminated spinach
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2006-spinach-recall_zps22808685.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2006-spinach-recall_zps22808685.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2006-spinach-recall_zps22808685.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Following the outbreak in 2006, the California Leafy Greens Handler Marketing Agreement (LGMA) was established in the spring of 2007. The LGMA, operating with oversight from the California Department of Food and Agriculture, provides a mechanism for verifying that farmers follow established food safety practices for lettuce, spinach and other leafy greens.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2005 BP Texas City Refinery Explosion
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          After the accident which killed 15 and injured 170, both the BP and the Chemical Safety and Hazard Investigation Board reports identified numerous technical and organizational failings at the refinery and within corporate BP.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2005-bp-texas-city-refinery-explosion_zpse4a242b2.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2005-bp-texas-city-refinery-explosion_zpse4a242b2.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2005-bp-texas-city-refinery-explosion_zpse4a242b2.jpg" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Organizational failings
          <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_City_Refinery_explosion">
           included
          </a>
          :
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          corporate cost-cutting, a failure to invest in the plant infrastructure, a lack of corporate oversight on both safety culture and major accident prevention programs, a focus on occupational safety and not process safety, a defective management of change process (which allowed the siting of contractor trailers too close to the ISOM process unit), the inadequate training of operators, a lack of competent supervision for start-up operations, poor communications between individuals and departments and the use of outdated and ineffective work procedures which were often not followed. Technical failings included a blowdown drum that was of insufficient size, a lack of preventative maintenance on safety critical systems, inoperative alarms and level sensors in the ISOM process unit and the continued use of outdated blowdown drum and stack technology when replacement with the safer flare option had been a feasible alternative for many years.
         </blockquote>
         It's a good thing BP learned their lesson after 2005.
         <p>
          <strong>
           2002-2004 Merck Vioxx
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          By the time Vioxx, approved by the FDA in 1999, was pulled off the market in 2004, nearly 25 million Americans had taken the drug.
         </p>
         <p>
          Internal
          <a href="http://online.wsj.com/news/articles/SB109926864290160719">
           Merck documents
          </a>
          show that the company knew about the problem at least as early as 2000, but continued to market the product as safe. Merck even provided an obstacle handling guide to counter doctor concerns of heart risk.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2004-merck-vioxx-sm_zpsb99447dd.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2004-merck-vioxx-sm_zpsb99447dd.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2004-merck-vioxx-sm_zpsb99447dd.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2001 Enron collapse
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          Enron hid failed deals and projects for years through the use of accounting loopholes and special purpose entities.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/2001-enron_political_cartoon_zpse58f6c70.gif.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo 2001-enron_political_cartoon_zpse58f6c70.gif" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/2001-enron_political_cartoon_zpse58f6c70.gif" width="550"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          The collapse of Enron led to the Sarbanes-Oxley Act. This legislation increased penalties for defrauding shareholders or tampering with records. The act also increased the accountability of auditing firms to remain unbiased and independent of their clients.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           2000 Firestone recalls 6.5 million tires
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          March 11, 1999In response to a Ford concern about tire separations on the Explorer, Bridgestone/Firestone sent a confidential memo to Ford claiming that less than 0.1 percent of all Wilderness tires (which are used on the Explorer) had been returned under warranty for all kinds of problems.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/firestone-tread-separation_zps8fc43696.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo firestone-tread-separation_zps8fc43696.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/firestone-tread-separation_zps8fc43696.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          August 9Firestone announced that it would recall about 6.5 million tires that were then on light trucks and SUVs because they had been implicated in more than 40 fatalities.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           What to do with this
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          Extensive lobbying, advertising, and education on behalf of certain business organizations is pushing the idea that markets have a built-in morality.
         </p>
         <p>
          Here's a great example from a site called
          <a href="http://studentsforliberty.org/morality-of-capitalism/">
           Students for Liberty
          </a>
          :
          <br/>
         </p>
         <blockquote>
          The task before us, thenif we wish to actualize the truly free social system that is laissez-faire capitalismis to provide and defend its moral justification. We must convince fellow students that capitalism is not just the most efficient system, but a virtuous one as well.
         </blockquote>
         Anyone who questions this morality is a liberal or in the view of
         <a href="http://www.foxbusiness.com/topics/the-government-is-killing-my-business.htm">
          some
         </a>
         :
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1350.photobucket.com/user/akadjian/media/gov_killing_my_business_640x360_zps82ffef8d.jpg.html" target="_blank">
           <img alt=" photo gov_killing_my_business_640x360_zps82ffef8d.jpg" border="0" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/gov_killing_my_business_640x360_zps82ffef8d.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          I've found, however, that it's pretty easy to make the case for regulation and ethics if you illustrate through a few examples (and keep partisanship out of it).
         </p>
         <p>
          To start with all you have to do is ask: what's the goal of a business?
         </p>
         <p>
          Obviously, it's to turn a profit.
         </p>
         <p>
          What's to prevent pursuing a profit at all costs? Especially if no regulations, enforcement, or penalties exist.
         </p>
         <p>
          We're frequently told: If only we could release business from the shackles of government and stop "forcing" them to obey regulations and laws, then the market would magically make everything better for people.
         </p>
         <p>
          However, when government deregulates or fails to properly enforce regulations, evidence overwhelmingly suggests that pursuit of profits trumps ethics, morality and the greater good. Not surprising given that this is the #1 stated priority.
         </p>
         <p>
          We simply need to recognize that markets have no implicit moral authority.
         </p>
         <p>
          We need to have a
          <a href="http://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2012/04/what-isnt-for-sale/308902/">
           debate about the moral limits of markets
          </a>
          . And we need to recognize that appropriate regulation, enforcement and good government are all components of a
          <a href="http://washingtonspectator.org/index.php/Politics/fairer-distribution-the-case-for-a-working-capitalism.html">
           working capitalism
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          Read the full
          <a href="http://www.oxfam.org/sites/www.oxfam.org/files/bp-working-for-few-political-capture-economic-inequality-200114-en.pdf">
           Oxfam report
          </a>
          (or summary of recommendations
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2014/01/22/1271695/-Now-that-you-know-85-people-own-more-than-half-the-world-here-s-what-to-do-about-it">
           here
          </a>
          ) for other recommendations on how to create a working capitalism including progressive taxation, cracking down on financial secrecy and tax dodging, and curbing the power of the wealthy to influence elections.
         </p>
         <p>
          ---
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/Little%20Book/little_book_sm_zps7eb5e66a.jpg" title="The Little Book of Revolution">
           <img align="left" alt="The Little Book of Revolution" src="http://i1350.photobucket.com/albums/p771/akadjian/Little%20Book/little_book_sm_zps7eb5e66a.jpg" width="70"/>
          </a>
          <br/>
          David Akadjian is the author of
          <a href="http://akadjian.com/">
           <em>
            <strong>
             The Little Book of Revolution: A Distributive Strategy for Democracy
            </strong>
           </em>
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          <a class="twitter-follow-button" defang_data-show-count="false" defang_data-size="large" href="https://twitter.com/akadjian">
           Follow @akadjian
          </a>
          <br/>
         </p>
        </div>
       </div>

          </p>

		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.

	If your diary is specific to a state, consider adding the state 
	(

          , etc).

	that don't fit in any of these tags. Don't worry if yours doesn't.

               In the former East Germany, clearly
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1271430/56445914#c197?mode=alone;showrate=1#c197">
                0+ / 0-
               </a>

              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               knowing the German rules for abbreviations and using hyphens whenever a person's name appears in street names. There is no street named after Karl Marx and other Communist figures in the former West Germany.

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              It was at Karl Marx Strae 231-235 near the Berlin-Neuklln S-Bhan &amp; U-Bhan station in the South-East suburbs, not Berlin metro area.
             </p>
             <p>
              It's no longer Walmart, they pulled out of Germany and sold most of the stores to Real, and what I could see from Google Street view this is now Real store so form there it was easy to find the
              <a href="http://www.real.de/markt-berlin-neukoelln">
               homepage
              </a>
              .
             </p>
             <p>
              I think the original photo
              <a href="hhttp://www.flickr.com/photos/hibou/8094868/">
               here
              </a>
              is from early 00's.
             </p>
             <p>
              Actually, I lived in Berlin for awhile in the 90's but seldom went to that area, just pass by in the train. In the US you would call that a "fly-over" town I think.
             </p>
             <p>
              Every West German city of size has a Siemens Strae and every East German City of size has a Karl Marx Strae.
             </p>

           <li id="c187">
            <div class="cx" id="cx56439945">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               Walmart left because they couldn't compete
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1271430/56439945#c187?mode=alone;showrate=1#c187">
                1+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:1099266">
                 Angry old lady
                </a>
               </dd>
              </dl>
             </div>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               There are mandated closing hours in Germany, so no 24-hour Walmarts to outlast the little guys. (No Sunday shopping, most stores are closed by 8 pm.)
              </p>
              <p>
               Products have to have a certain markup over wholesale, so loss leaders are banned and there is much less undercutting the little guy.
              </p>
              <p>
               And, this kills me, they used to make Walmart workers sing some sort of company loyalty song before shifts. Yeah... forced loyalty singing goes over REALLY well in Germany.
              </p>
              <p>
               The Walmart where I live (2nd largest city in Germany) had crappy products that were relatively expensive. They had some fun American food that wasn't elsewhere, so I'd go in there when I was a bit homesick.
              </p>
              <p>
               No one was surprised when they pulled out.
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>
              <p class="cb">
               by

              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1271430/56445942#c198?mode=alone;showrate=1#c198">
                0+ / 0-

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               with two or more names. if only one name like "Siemens" is used, then it will be written together with "strasse", as in Siemensstrasse.

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Great diary. Great pictures. Great topic for discussion.
           </p>
           <p>
            But in your discussion of the morality of markets, I believe you have forgotten an important picture: that of the markets buying the law-makers, judges, and yes presidents.
           </p>
           <p>
            Indeed, it is exactly because markets are allowed to buy law-makers, judges, and presidents that our water is turning brown and oil-fouled; that pharmaceutical companies sell use dangerous pills; that manufacturers are allowed to create unsafe conditions for their workers; etc.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            "The fool doth think he is wise: the wise man knows himself to be a fool" - W. Shakespeare

            <a href="/user/uid:311488">
             Hugh Jim Bissell

            on
            <a href="/comments/1271430/52539834#c3">
             Mon Feb 03, 2014 at 06:35:39 AM PST
            </a>

           <li id="c164">
            <div class="cx" id="cx52566227">
             <h5>
              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               My biggest disappointment was discovering that SCO
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1271430/52566227#c164?mode=alone;showrate=1#c164">
                0+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               the Supreme Court and its wisdom had been infected and the legally correct answer and the decision that was handed down no longer resembled one another at all (in some very important circumstances) But this was later determined to (more likely then not) to be the result of blackmail versus the market.
              </p>
              <p>
               Of all of the various markets in your diary here NONE of the examples portray a market free of governments heavy handed fingerprints ...perhaps a better title would be something like "25 Examples of The Government Influence on the Markets"
              </p>
              <p>
               My last observation is that your problems seem to be with the how and not the what a marketplace produces. Almost all of the criticism of markets results from widespread disapproval of the morality of the behavior that drives the market process, very much independently of the outcomes that are generated. Given the prevailing view of duty-based morality, even those (like alot of you) who accept the superiority of markets at generating material comforts commonly see that superiority as so morally tainted that they are sympathetic to political action to restrict normal market practices at the cost of considerable market efciencies.
              </p>
              <p>
               The instinctive hostility toward the lack of morality (and
               <br/>
               immorality) widely seen as motivating the market process commonly undermines appreciation for markets no matter how desirable their outcomes. There is a a widespread view of morality that predisposes most people to see
               <br/>
               markets as fundamentally immoral. Why not start by accepting the dominant view of moral behavior as a legitimate one, while recognizing that the superiority of markets is the result oftheir ability to generate desirable outcomes without relying on what is widely seen as moral behavior
               <br/>
              </p>
             </div>
             <div class="cf">
              <p class="sig">
              </p>

           <ul class="cm i1" id="k52566227">
            <li id="c170">
             <div class="cx" id="cx52566761">
              <h5>
               <a class="de">
               </a>
               <span class="cu">
                The morality of the market place
               </span>
               <span class="crd ntb">
                (
                <a href="/comments/1271430/52566761#c170?mode=alone;showrate=1#c170">
                 1+ / 0-
                </a>
                )
               </span>
              </h5>
              <div class="crs">
               <dl>
                <dt>
                 Recommended by:
                </dt>
                <dd>
                 <a href="/user/uid:990271">
                  enufenuf
                 </a>
                </dd>
               </dl>
              </div>
              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                The morality of the market place is driven by profit. Large corporations have pushed their legislators to introduce legislation which legitimizes profit as the primary goal of large corporations.
               </p>
               <p>
                The results are the expected ones. New CEOs come in and look for ways to increase profit -- a major one of which is cost cutting-- buying cheaper materials, improving the manufacturing process (or it's equivalent in non-manufacturing industries), cheapening the costs of labor -- and the ones listed here cut costs of safety and the safety infrastructure.
               </p>
               <p>
                I argue that all these disasters are not accidents -- they are the results of calculated gambles by the CEOs which failed. The clever (not intelligent, but clever) CEOs do the most socialist corporate thing (also listed above) -- they privatize the profits and socialize the risk. Which means that we, the poor and middle class taxpayers pay the major part of their gambles.
               </p>
               <p>
                We financed Romney that way to the tune of well over $10 million, we are still paying for BP and it's Gulf profiteering. We paid for Enron's failed gamble -- and the list goes on--- and on -- and on.
               </p>
               <p>
                We have these tactics enshrined in our laws -- not because these laws are good laws but because big moneyed corporations bought legislators (including various presidents) to make the laws which freely permit them to gamble like this.
               </p>
               <p>
                We have these tactics enshrined in our laws -- because we have not been diligent in regulating the "freedom" of the market place to gamble like this with the lives and futures of us, our families, our communities and our world.
               </p>
               <p>
                Welcome to the world of global climate change caused by unregulated markets and lack of responsibility of us all, but particularly by large corporations guided by greed.
               </p>
              </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             Well said. And I like your phrasing of "done right".
            </p>
            <p>
             Free marketeers argue about the burden of regulation and there is some economic truth to the idea that you can't regulate everything.
            </p>
            <p>
             However, when we're lurching from one crisis to the next caused, each caused by the almost complete lack of regulation, it's pretty easy to make the case that we've gone too far in assuming markets have a built-in morality.
            </p>

             <span class="cu">
              You forgot one
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1271430/52541153#c63?mode=alone;showrate=1#c63">
               9+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>

               <a href="/user/uid:918758">

               </a>

               <a href="/user/uid:48263">
                caul
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              The Enron Loophole and the speculation of oil prices by hedge funds in 2007 drove the price of oil up by 100%.
             </p>
             <p>
              At its peak, and just prior to the great recession of 2008, the United States public had increased its daily cost of gasoline by almost 800 million dollars PER DAY.
             </p>
             <p>
              the vast majority of these costs were due to speculation by hedge funds, cornering the commodities futures market. Only after the closing of the Enron loophole and the collapse of the economy did the prices go back down.
             </p>
             <p>
              <a href="http://www.cga.ct.gov/2011/rpt/2011-R-0290.htm">
               http://www.cga.ct.gov/...
              </a>
             </p>

              And this does not in any diminish the tremendous accomplishment of diary. Indeed, the diarist's inclusion of some of the lesser-known cases (like the toy that turned into the date-rape drug when ingested) shows just how pervasive the problem is.
             </p>
            </div>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toxics_Release_Inventory">
                Union Carbide
               </a>
               plants absolutely should
               <strong>
                not
               </strong>
               be forgotten. Even though the 1985 WV incident was smaller, it was memorable to me since it was from a similar plant performing a similar function right here in the USA (w/ our "
               <em>
                so
               </em>
               -superior" regulatory framework, oversight, laws, and "society") and had the horrific Bhopal incident as a "wake-up call" precedent.
              </p>
              <p>
               It struck me even then (and still does) that those who bore/bear the price of such "
               <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Externality">
                economic externalities
               </a>
               " are so often those w/ the least power.
              </p>
              <p>
               Thanks for the (sad) reminder.

              <a class="de">
              </a>
              <span class="cu">
               The story of Bhopali is easily lost, but ..
              </span>
              <span class="crd ntb">
               (
               <a href="/comments/1271430/52541653#c78?mode=alone;showrate=1#c78">
                11+ / 0-
               </a>
               )
              </span>
             </h5>
             <div class="crs">
              <dl>
               <dt>
                Recommended by:
               </dt>
               <dd>
                <a href="/user/uid:82747">
                 bartcopfan
                </a>
                ,
                <a href="/user/uid:330318">
                 JerryNA
                </a>
                ,
                <a href="/user/uid:255072">
                 jan4insight
                </a>

                <a href="/user/uid:306301">

                </a>

                <a href="/user/uid:41957">

                </a>

                </a>

                <a href="/user/uid:918758">

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               it has been documented in a film from Van Maximilian Carlson, BHOPALI. The documentary is available on
               <a href="http://www.hulu.com/watch/525960">
                Hulu
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Bhopali-Sanjay-Verma/dp/B0082WVFUC/ref=sr_1_2_vod_0_ren?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1391449964&amp;sr=8-2&amp;keywords=bhopali">
                Amazon Prime
               </a>
               and
               <a href="http://www.indiepixfilms.com/film/5290">
                IndiePix Films
               </a>
               . The film features Sanjay Verma, who was a baby and escaped the disaster that night, now an activist for recovery and problem solving. The report has won many substantial awards -- see list below -- and is well worth 80 minutes of your time and attention. The complicity of the US Government -- include our Justice system and Senate -- with its major industrial companies, Union Carbide and Dow Chemical, is so appalling that it goes beyond anger to inspire a depressing view of social morality. Bhopali, 27 years ago, was a warning of what was to come.
              </p>
              <p>
               Awards
              </p>

              </p>

              </p>

              </p>

               <br/>
               2011 Slamdance Film Festival (Park City, United States)
               <br/>

         <li id="c67">
          <div class="cx" id="cx52541267">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             I don't particularly object to pink slime.
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1271430/52541267#c67?mode=alone;showrate=1#c67">
              6+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:1283">
               Joe Bob
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:330318">
               JerryNA
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:73842">
               4Freedom
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:90468">
               milkbone
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:918758">
               thanatokephaloides
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:48263">
               caul
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             Yes, it's disgusting, but that's neither here nor there. If you watched the entire process of a cow being transformed from a living animal into a steak, there'd be plenty to be revolted at.
            </p>
            <p>
             Given the immense environmental cost of beef, it makes sense to make as much use of the carcass as possible -- if we can't find other uses for it. The main problem with pink slime is the risk of bacterial contamination, which is why it is treated with ammonia (gaseous, not liquid as in Jamie Oliver's demonstration). The ammonia residue itself doesn't present any real health threat in the concentrations present in the final product, but if you want to be super-cautious, then use citric acid.
            </p>
            <p>
             I don't have a problem with hamburger containing ten or fifteen percent of this stuff, as long as it is clearly labelled as "containing meat byproducts". "Meat byproducts" seems to me to be a reasonable compromise between the sensational "pink slime" and the Orwellian "lean finely textured beef".
            </p>
            <p>
             If you are really concerned about industrial beef, I don't see how regular ground beef is necessarily any "better" than pink slime. If you want a better product, it makes more sense to obtain beef by small local producers, who are more likely to provide you with a natural, sustainably produced product.
            </p>
           </div>

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              There isnt a lot of logical consistency between being willing to eat highly processed ground beef and being grossed out by pink slime.
             </p>
             <p>
              I dont know that pink slime is even especially relevant to the contamination issue. Whether the slime is in it or not, processed beef is going to contain meat from multiple animals and thereby have an increased risk of contamination. If someone really cares about this issue and really loves hamburger they should buy a whole cut of beef and have a butcher grind it up. That way you know what you are getting.
             </p>

           </p>
           <p>
            Always, in any conversation you have, remind people who it is that is truly screwing them over. It ain't the government. Remind them their phone reception sucks and costs way too much, their cable tv is expensive and full of crap, can't get the flight you want anymore because there are 4 airlines now and the fares are higher and higher and higher.....want to buy a car? Find 20 grand because no one makes a cheaper one and it's not so the workers can get paid too much. Remind them...again and again and again. Obscene profit is not the proper incentive. But because some have elevated it to a position way above where it belongs, it has consumed us as a nation.
           </p>
          </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             Well said!
            </p>
            <p>
             I can sympathize with the anger from people against the government because they see how government officials are bought and sold.
            </p>
            <p>
             This is why I find it very easy to talk to Libertarians and people who identify with the Tea Party. It pisses both of us off.
            </p>
            <p>
             I just use things like this to make the case for good government. Not "no government".
            </p>
            <p>
             We want a less corrupt government, a government working for us, rather than what some corporations have been arguing for for the past 30 years: no government.
            </p>
            <p>
             I've found that if you keep the focus on ideas and economics, you can win people over. Because I'll be honest, I don't really care who comes out against supply-side economics.
            </p>
            <p>
             Just so long as the solutions they're proposing aren't more supply-side economics.

            <span class="cu">
             There is, but it's not what most people think
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1271430/52540891#c52?mode=alone;showrate=1#c52">
              9+ / 0-
             </a>
             )

              <a href="/user/uid:327746">

             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             Here's a great video of John Geanakoplos, an economist at Yale, demonstrating what economists mean when they say "invisible hand"
            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="http://oyc.yale.edu/economics/econ-251/lecture-1#ch6">
              http://oyc.yale.edu/...
             </a>
            </p>
            <p>
             You don't have to watch the whole thing, just the last 15 minutes or so. On the right, click on
             <strong>
              An Experiment of the Financial Market
             </strong>
             .
            </p>
            <p>
             The problem is that the religion of capitalism is different than the study of economics.
            </p>
            <p>
             In the religion, "invisible hand' means markets will do everything including slice your bread. In economics, "invisible hand" means that markets will settle on a product distribution and prices.
            </p>
            <p>
             Settling on a product distribution and prices, however, says nothing about whether the distribution and pricing will be good for people.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
            </p>
            <p class="cb">
             by
             <a href="/user/uid:319630">
              akadjian
             </a>
             on
             <a href="/comments/1271430/52540891#c52">
              Mon Feb 03, 2014 at 08:48:08 AM PST
             </a>
            </p>
            <p class="cl">
             [
             <a href="#c15">
              Parent
             </a>
             ]
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>
         <ul class="cm i1" id="k52540891">
          <li id="c65">
           <div class="cx" id="cx52541230">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              "In the long run we are all dead"
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1271430/52541230#c65?mode=alone;showrate=1#c65">
               4+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:330318">

               <a href="/user/uid:918758">

               </a>

               <a href="/user/uid:48263">

              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <blockquote>
              In economics, "invisible hand" means that markets will settle on a product distribution and prices.
             </blockquote>
             I'm still waiting for any market to settle on any product distribution, or any pricing.
             <p>
              It's not a closed, equilibrium system. "Energy", in the form human inventiveness, natural disaters, and other disruptions, is always being injected. These forces overwhelm whatever modest pressure some hypothetical invisible hand may or may not be delivering. It's chaos out there!
             </p>
             <p>
              I'm 100% on board with the idea that
              <strong>
               <em>
                our
               </em>
              </strong>
              hands ought to be the ones on the rudders, in the form of labor laws, minimum wages, etc. I have no faith in invisible hands, of whatever description.
             </p>
             <p>
              That said, I'll enjoy watching the vid this evening. Thanks for the link!
             </p>
            </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             How long are you willing to work to change it? That's the question everyone needs to ask themselves.
            </p>
            <p>
             I get on a couple of my neighbors all the time. They bitch and complain that we have no fire hydrants near us, but never, ever go to any of the city council meetings. Same with parents at the schools.....never see them at a school board meeting, or a parent night.
            </p>
            <p>
             Being a citizen is work and too few are willing to put it in. That's what it boils down to. All the "old folks" who get out and vote....well, that's experience and wisdom on full display.
            </p>
            <p>
             Local is the place to start. Most of the members of Congress cut their teeth on local corruption.

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            and great pictures to drive it home.
           </p>
           <p>
            I have heard that even Adam Smith, the father of capitalism, argued that the free market must operate within a moral framework, or it becomes a rapacious beast that devours all the other parts of the economy.
            <br/>
            Believe we have all seen that validated over and over again.
           </p>
           <p>
            As you stated, corporations and businesses exist for one primary reason, to make money.
            <br/>
            While it would be nice if the owners operated with the good of the public and their workers in mind, that is not their chief mission.
            <br/>
            So that is why there are governments, to balance the drive to maximize profits, with the often negative impacts that can have.
            <br/>
            And let's not forget that corporations are not natural entities. They are creations of the state, governments pass the laws that control the setup and operation of corporations. They do not exist without governments.
           </p>
          </div>

           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             He believed that businessmen, left to themselves, would write laws and regulations which favored themselves.
             <br/>
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             The proposal of any new law or regulation of commerce which comes from [businessmen] ... comes from an order of men ... who have generally an interest to deceive and even to oppress the public, and who accordingly have, upon many occasions, both deceived and oppressed it.
            </blockquote>
            Adam Smith, The Wealth of Nations
            <p>
             <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Worse-Than-You-Think-Washingtons/dp/0983879710">
              <em>
               Worse than You Think: The Real Economy Hidden Beneath Washingtons Rigged Statistics, And Where To Go From Here
              </em>
             </a>
             , by Keith Quincy.

          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            If knowledge is power and power corrupts, does that mean that knowledge corrupts?
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:70396">
             AoT
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1271430/52540385#c27">
             Mon Feb 03, 2014 at 07:55:12 AM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>

        <ul class="cm i1" id="k52540385">
         <li id="c59">
          <div class="cx" id="cx52541083">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Those who argue for "free markets" believe ...
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1271430/52541083#c59?mode=alone;showrate=1#c59">
              3+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:120685">
               happymisanthropy
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:330318">
               JerryNA
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:918758">
               thanatokephaloides
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             there is a natural, built-in morality.
            </p>
            <p>
             You hear this expressed in phrases like "the market will always regulate itself" and "free markets".
            </p>
            <p>
             They believe that the pursuit of selfishness always leads to a greater good.
            </p>
            <p>
             In this world, the 85 people who own more than the 3.5 billion poorest are morally doing the right thing because they are acting out of selfishness.
            </p>
            <p>
             In this world, the people at Merck are doing the right moral thing because they were acting selfishly.
            </p>
            <p>
             I don't doubt that people arguing for "free markets" personally don't believe in slavery. I'm simply saying that the market itself has no built-in morality as is often claimed.
            </p>
           </div>

            <p class="sig">

              </blockquote>
              Capitalism seems to do fine with slave labor or convict labor. I'm gonna have to ask you to justify this statement.
              <p>
               To the extent that capitalism disparages slavery, it's because slave owners are stuck caring for elderly slaves from whom productivity can no longer be extracted, which in many cases pushes the net cost of slave labor above the Ricardo equilibrium cost of free labor.

              <div class="ct">
               <p>
                slavery. And clearly capitalism doesn't have a problem with slavery, capitalism was built on slavery. Capitalism isn't about free markets necessarily. But if one actor in a market is under legal obligation to provide labor for no price, which is what slavery is, then it's no longer a free market.
               </p>
               <p>
                Capitalism loves "free" markets but the theoretical free market of the libertarian is a myth, it simply can't be created. Which isn't surprising given the foolish myths that libertarianism is based on. The problem with free markets isn't that they are inherently bad, it's that they're only possible under perfect conditions, which means they never exist. But this fact eludes libertarians.
               </p>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               A market certainly can be free if people are enslaved, because what "free market" means is "the people who run the market (i.e., the wealthy) are not interfered with by the government or anybody else telling them what they can do with their money." Including buying or selling slaves, if that's what they want to do.
              </p>
              <p>
               Where I think you're going wrong, and it's no wonder b/c it's built into the "free market" argument, is in what constitutes
               <strong>
                a person
               </strong>
               under this philosophy. Capitalism doesn't want to talk about that much, and neither do advocates of the "free market," but the only people who really count as people under this philosophy are the ones with lots of money. They're the ones who get to be "free" and operate "freely" in the "free market;" everybody else gets to be commodities to be bought and sold, servants who are annoying but necessary and should be paid as little as possible, and, well, waste product. These days more and more of us fall into the final category.
              </p>

             Adam Smith was no con man. He was a moral philosopher who used the term exactly ONCE in a very long and detailed book. The con men came later, and are those that take Adam Smith out of context, omitting:
             <br/>
            </p>
            <blockquote>
             "People of the same trade seldom meet together, even for merriment and diversion, but the conversation ends in a conspiracy against the public, or in some contrivance to raise prices. "
            </blockquote>
            From Joan Robinson:
            <br/>
            <blockquote>
             The purpose of studying economics is not to acquire a set of ready-made answers to economic questions, but to learn how to avoid being deceived by economists.
             <p>
              " It [orthodox traditional economics ]was a plan for explaining to the privileged class that their position was morally right and was necessary for the welfare of society."
             </p>
            </blockquote>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
            </p>

              </strong>

              <strong>

              </strong>

              <strong>
               other
              </strong>
              aspects of what we consider to be "regulation" (safety, health, working conditions, taxation, etc.). Only a hardcore Randroid would think otherwise.
             </p>
             <p>
              Of course, it's possible that the "Masters of the Universe", to-hell-with-you-Jack-I-got-mine aspect of MBA-school didn't take....
             </p>
             <p>
              But, as usual, a major takeaway is to be careful (in debate, and the like) to clarify the definitions of terms. If a conservative talks about "regulations" "killing the market", we can call them out: do they mean the worker and public safety regulations? or the anti-slavery or anti-child-labor regulations? or the don't-poison-the environment and people downstream regulations? the anti-collusion/cartel regulations?
             </p>
             <p>
              I figure prostitution and the drug trade are the purest free markets there are--are those
              <strong>
               really
              </strong>
              what the conservative wants to emulate?
             </p>

              <strong>
               your
              </strong>

              <strong>
               best understood
              </strong>
              as
              <strong>
               millionaires and billionaires
              </strong>
              . Unfortunately, on economics, lots of working- and middle-class people think Rs are talking to
              <strong>
               them
              </strong>

             </a>

             <a href="/user/uid:97252">

             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:100012">

             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <blockquote>
            To start with all you have to do is ask: what's the goal of a business?
            <p>
             Obviously, it's to turn a profit.
            </p>
           </blockquote>
           You are conflating "business" with "capitalism", and they are not the same.
           <p>
            The purpose of "business" is to enhance trade; trade is not about profit, per se, but about the distribution of goods, services and necessities from those who make them to those who want or need them, to the benefit of all.
           </p>
           <p>
            Capitalism is about profit, even if it is detrimental to trade or society overall.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt1640459/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">

           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Thanks
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1271430/52540486#c36?mode=alone;showrate=1#c36">
             8+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">

             <a href="/user/uid:330318">

             </a>

             </a>

             <a href="/user/uid:918758">

             </a>

          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            My favorite example is the rise in healthcare costs. Since people are ultimately willing to sacrifice their entire net worth to, for example, obtain an operation that will vastly improve or save their lives, the market happily sets higher and higher prices as a result. This of course distorts the amount of money people have to spend on other things.
           </p>
           <p>
            It cannot be repeated enough that "free market" only works for commodities where demand and supply are both rational, and where true cost is factored into the equation. The demand for healthcare could not be any less rational.
           </p>

           </div>
          </div>
         </li>
        </ul>
        <li id="c40">
         <div class="cx" id="cx52540568">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            The purpose of a business is NOT to turn a profit.
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1271430/52540568#c40?mode=alone;showrate=1#c40">
             6+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:255072">
              jan4insight
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:982541">
              socialismorbarbarism
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:319630">
              akadjian
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:97252">
              sfbob
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:198313">
              tardis10
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:330318">
              JerryNA
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            The purpose of a business is to provide a good or service to the wider community that an individual cannot provide on his own. We permit incorporation so that individuals can work together beyond simple personal arrangements, and insulate their private lives from creditors should their business fail. Any profit that the business owner or corporate shareholders reap above and beyond self support is bonus, not the purpose of the business.
           </p>
           <p>
            The profit-above-all mantra is corrosive to the fundamental purpose of the tools of capitalism - the maximum benefit of society. This is a moral choice that we have allowed to be made wrongly. It must end.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:432179">
             Orakio
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1271430/52540568#c40">
             Mon Feb 03, 2014 at 08:15:51 AM PST
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>

            </span>

            </p>
            <p>
             <a href="http://www.colorado.edu/studentgroups/libertarians/issues/friedman-soc-resp-business.html">
              The beginning of the end: Friedman sets the moral avalanche in motion
             </a>
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
             I tried to go online to find a similar bear head...but when I searched Big Bear Head it gave me a San Diego craigslist ad entitled Big Bear needs some quick head now and then I just decided to never go on the internet again.--Jenny Lawson
            </p>
            <p class="cb">
             by
             <a href="/user/uid:212680">
              SouthernLiberalinMD
             </a>
             on
             <a href="/comments/1271430/52543542#c105">

             </a>
            </p>
            <p class="cl">
             [
             <a href="#c40">

             </a>

            </p>
           </div>
          </div>
         </li>
         <ul class="cm i1" id="k52543542">
          <li id="c131">
           <div class="cx" id="cx52547825">
            <h5>
             <a class="de">
             </a>
             <span class="cu">
              I've never read any Friedman before.
             </span>
             <span class="crd ntb">
              (
              <a href="/comments/1271430/52547825#c131?mode=alone;showrate=1#c131">
               2+ / 0-
              </a>
              )
             </span>
            </h5>
            <div class="crs">
             <dl>
              <dt>
               Recommended by:
              </dt>
              <dd>
               <a href="/user/uid:918758">
                thanatokephaloides
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="/user/uid:212680">
                SouthernLiberalinMD
               </a>
              </dd>
             </dl>
            </div>
            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              Now, I'm sorry that I have, and deeply mourn the publication of it.
             </p>
             <p>
              The act of turning a profit is not, in itself, evil. But in the process of doing so, a business must adequately recompense all of those who have contributed to it. This includes adequate pay for labor. This includes not soiling and poisoning the surrounding environment. This is not charity; this is honoring all the contracts that a business has made, both written and implied by the very act of incorporating and selecting a community in which to fulfill the corporate charter.
             </p>
             <p>
              The customer comes first - without them, the corporation has no reason to exist. The suppliers of materiel, labor, and community(which gives land, water, etc.) comes next, for without them, the customer can certainly not be served, and their contribution is a debt that must be serviced. Capital comes last, for several reasons: First, we permit the legal construct of the corporation to exist only because it can benefit society. Second, because it provides its aid to the corporation but once per share issued; labor, supply, and rent are required in the day to day operation, and without their services, the company fails. When a shareholder wants out, he sells his share, and no one at the company cares, unless there is enough shift to significantly alter shareholder's votes.
             </p>
             <p>
              While it is fine enough to speak of fulfilling a duty that a business owes to its suppliers, laborers, and community as being a social good, we need to also name the failure to fulfill those duties as what they are: Theft and fraudulent breach of contract.
             </p>
             <p>
              Corporations are chartered by the government to benefit we, the people. When the corporation becomes harmful to we, the people, then it is a moral obligation upon the government to revoke the charter and "kill" the corporation.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="cf">
             <p class="sig">
             </p>
             <p class="cb">
              by
              <a href="/user/uid:432179">
               Orakio
              </a>
              on
              <a href="/comments/1271430/52547825#c131">
               Mon Feb 03, 2014 at 09:45:52 PM PST
              </a>
             </p>
             <p class="cl">
              [
              <a href="#c105">
               Parent
              </a>
              ]
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>

              <p>
               My personal take on it is that keeping those contracts is not only a duty but also a practical necessity; in other words, what's being framed as altruism, and in Friedman's terms a wrongheaded, misguided, perhaps even immoral form of altruism, is actually system maintenance, and anybody who doesn't understand that shouldn't have authority over a corner grocery store, much less the finances of the world.
              </p>

               Nihilism is not a best practices manual.

            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Pink slime is mechanically separated chicken
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1271430/52542623#c96?mode=alone;showrate=1#c96">
              3+ / 0-

              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:73842">

              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:918758">
               thanatokephaloides
              </a>
             </dd>
